- Completion re-audit (2026-06-22, refreshed 2026-06-23): the previous reopened snapshot correctly caught stale open rows, but the later continuation closed the main selected mathematical blockers: endpoint-aware Riesz-Thorin, source-facing SVD predicate, Theorem 6.4 radius-limit wrappers, Lemma 6.6 real-rectangular rank-sensitive packaging, Problem 6.1 equality packaging, and the fixed-shape Problem 6.5 bare unitary-invariant norm theorem. The remaining Chapter 6 rows are generic source-notation/API polish or optional family-level coherence wrappers rather than active selected mathematical blockers, so the selected-core open-row count is now recorded as zero.

- Current continuation update (2026-06-22, Problem 6.1 Table 6.2 `M/S/F/2` comparison layer): the source table entries involving entrywise max norm `M`, entrywise sum norm `S`, Frobenius norm `F`, and Euclidean operator norm `2` now have checked local comparison theorems. New declarations `complexMatrixEntrywiseMaxNorm`, `complexMatrixEntrywiseSumNorm`, `complexMatrixEntrywiseSumNorm_le_card_mul_entrywiseMaxNorm`, `complexMatrixEntrywiseMaxNorm_le_frobenius`, `complexMatrixFrobenius_le_entrywiseSumNorm`, `complexMatrixEntrywiseSumNorm_le_sqrt_card_mul_frobenius`, `complexMatrixFrobenius_le_sqrt_card_mul_entrywiseMaxNorm`, `complexMatrixEntrywiseMaxNorm_le_op2`, and `complexMatrixEntrywiseSumNorm_le_sqrt_card_rank_mul_op2` close the deterministic inequality layer behind several Table 6.2 entries, including the printed rank-sensitive `S` versus `2` constant. The remaining source clauses in Problem 6.1 are the rank-one attainability assertions for the table entries other than `alpha_{S,2}`, the real square Hadamard iff equality case for `alpha_{S,2}`, and the complex roots-of-unity/Vandermonde equality example. No new GPT-5.5 Pro browser call was needed because these were finite-sum, coordinate, Frobenius, and Cauchy-Schwarz/order consequences over the existing checked norm layer.

- Current continuation update (2026-06-22, Problem 6.1 rank-one `xy^T` witness values): the prescribed source witnesses `x,y in {e_j,e}` now have checked raw values for the entrywise max norm `M`, entrywise sum norm `S`, and Frobenius norm `F`. `complexMatrixRankOne` models `x y^T`; `complexMatrixEntrywiseSumNorm_rankOne` proves the product formula `||xy^T||_S = ||x||_1 ||y||_1`; `complexMatrixFrobeniusSq_rankOne` proves the squared Frobenius product formula; and the four standard/all-ones witness families are evaluated by the `complexMatrixEntrywiseSumNorm_rankOne_*`, `complexMatrixFrobenius_rankOne_*`, and `complexMatrixEntrywiseMaxNorm_rankOne_*` theorem families. This is a reusable attainability dependency for Table 6.2, but it does not yet close the full table-wide sharpness statement because the operator-2, endpoint matrix-norm, and equality-characterization clauses still need to be connected.

- Current continuation update (2026-06-22, Problem 6.1 rank-one operator-2 witness values): the same standard/all-ones rank-one witnesses now also have checked Euclidean operator-2 values. `complexMatrixOp2_rankOne_standard_standard`, `complexMatrixOp2_rankOne_const_standard`, `complexMatrixOp2_rankOne_standard_const`, and `complexMatrixOp2_rankOne_const_const` prove the values `1`, `sqrt m`, `sqrt n`, and `sqrt(m*n)` for `e_i e_j^T`, `e e_j^T`, `e_i e^T`, and `e e^T`, respectively. The upper bounds come from the Frobenius values, and the lower bounds use the operator-2 bound on a standard-basis or all-ones source vector. This closes the raw `2`-norm witness layer for Table 6.2; the remaining Problem 6.1 sharpness work is connecting endpoint induced `1` and `infinity` values and the special `alpha_{S,2}` equality cases.

- Current continuation update (2026-06-22, Problem 6.1 rank-one endpoint induced-norm witness values): the concrete matrix `1`-norm and infinity-norm values are now checked for the same standard/all-ones rank-one witnesses. `complexMatrixOneNorm_rankOne_*` proves the column-sum values `1`, `m`, `1`, and `m`; `complexMatrixInfNorm_rankOne_*` proves the row-sum values `1`, `1`, `n`, and `n`. Together with the previous `M/S/F/2` theorem families, this supplies all raw norm values needed for the Table 6.2 rank-one sharpness witnesses other than the excluded `alpha_{S,2}` case. Remaining Problem 6.1 work is table-wide quotient/source-packaging and the real Hadamard/complex roots-of-unity equality clauses for `alpha_{S,2}`.

- Current continuation update (2026-06-22, Problem 6.1 rank-one source-facing profile package): the four prescribed rank-one witnesses are now collected into checked source-facing profile wrappers. `HighamProblem61RankOneNormProfile` records the six concrete norm values `1`, `infinity`, `M`, `S`, `F`, and `2` for a witness matrix; `HighamProblem61RankOneTableProfiles` packages the four witness cases `e_i e_j^T`, `e e_j^T`, `e_i e^T`, and `e e^T`; and `highamProblem61_rankOne_table_profiles` proves the complete nonempty-dimensional witness table from the individual raw-value theorems. - Current continuation update (2026-06-22, Problem 6.1 rank-one quotient package): the rank-one profiles are now connected to actual Table 6.2 sharpness quotients for all rank-one-attained entries except `S/2`. `complexMatrixRank_rankOne_standard_standard` proves that `e_i e_j^T` has local matrix rank `1`, which closes the rank-sensitive `F/2` quotient wrapper. `HighamProblem61NormQuotientWitness` records a positive denominator norm and an equality `numerator = alpha * denominator`; `HighamProblem61RankOneTableQuotientWitnesses` packages the `e_i e_j^T`, `e e_j^T`, `e_i e^T`, and `e e^T` witnesses across the rank-one-attained `1`, `2`, `infinity`, `F`, `M`, and `S` quotient entries; and `highamProblem61_rankOne_table_quotient_witnesses` proves the package for nonempty dimensions. - Current continuation update (2026-06-22, Problem 6.1 real Hadamard `S/2` quotient witness): the real square Hadamard forward equality example for the rank-sensitive `alpha_{S,2}` row is now checked. `IsRealHadamardMatrix.complex_transpose_mul_self` proves `H^T H = n I` after complexification; `IsRealHadamardMatrix.complexMatrixRank_eq` proves full rank; `IsRealHadamardMatrix.complexMatrixEntrywiseSumNorm_eq` proves `||H||_S = n^2`; `IsRealHadamardMatrix.complexMatrixOp2_eq_sqrt` proves `||H||_2 = sqrt n`; `highamProblem61_s2_hadamard_calc` closes the scalar square-root arithmetic; and `highamProblem61_hadamard_s2_quotient_witness` packages `||H||_S = sqrt(n*n*rank(H)) ||H||_2`. No new GPT-5.5 Pro browser call was needed because the route was direct finite-dimensional matrix inverse/rank algebra from the existing Hadamard orthogonality predicate.

- Selected-scope continuation note (2026-06-21, source-facing Riesz-Thorin wrapper): the finite-real analytic-parameterized Riesz-Thorin route now reaches `IsComplexMatrixLpNormValue` and `complexMatrixLpNormOfReal` through `isComplexMatrixLpNormValue_le_rieszThorin_finite_dual_normer_of_endpoint_values` and `complexMatrixLpNormOfReal_le_rieszThorin_finite_dual_normer`. This improves the (6.18)-(6.20) status from "analytic proof route open" to "source-facing finite-real wrapper closed"; endpoint/unified `LpInterpolationData` packaging and printed specializations remain open.
- Selected-scope continuation note (2026-06-21/22): Problem 6.5's local real rectangular Frobenius/operator-2 product inequality is closed by the MatrixAlgebra theorem family, and the source complex Frobenius/operator-2 product inequality is closed by `highamProblem65_complexFrobenius_triple_mul_le`. The product theorem is also closed for fixed-shape and shape-changing operator-ideal interfaces by `highamProblem65_fixedOperatorIdealNorm_triple_mul_le` and `highamProblem65_operatorIdealNorm_triple_mul_le`. - Selected-scope continuation note (2026-06-21/22): Equation (6.14)'s abstract Schneider-Strang max-ratio formula, equation (6.15)'s finite p/q sharp-ratio instantiation, the local matrix `p`-norm unit-sphere/nonzero-ratio wrappers, the concrete local `complexMatrixLpNorm` and finite-real `complexMatrixLpNormOfReal` wrappers, the endpoint-aware Riesz-Thorin theorem, the main SVD/rank/Frobenius scaffold through concrete local unitary factorization, the source-facing SVD factor predicate, the local perturbation-limit condition-number API, and the older real-rectangular rank-sensitive Lemma 6.6 wrapper are now formalized. No selected work from this blocker cluster remains open; only optional source-notation/downstream variants remain.
- Selected-scope continuation note (2026-06-21): Theorem 6.4 now also has the checked local linearized inverse-condition bridge recommended by the completed GPT-5.5 Pro consultation. `mixedInverseSandwichUnitImageValue_max_eq_square` packages the derivative sandwich max `s^2`, and `mixedInverseLinearizedConditionValue_eq_conditionNumberProduct` records the relative linearized value as the product-form condition number. The exact inverse perturbation identity, the rearranged first-order error identity, the `s^2 * d^2 * b` remainder bound, the normalized `O(d)` error bound, the nonlinear upper amplification estimate `a*s*(1 + d*b)`, the conditional lower amplification estimate `a*s*(1 - d*b)`, the scaled linearized-sandwich witness package `exists_inverseSandwich_scaled_normValue_eq_square_mul`, its indexed family form `exists_inverseSandwich_scaled_normValue_family_eq_square_mul`, the fixed-scale predicate-level supremum squeeze `mixedInverseRelativeAmplificationAtScale_sup_squeeze_of_linearized`, the convergence-budget estimate `mixedInverseRelativeAmplificationAtScale_sup_abs_sub_condition_le`, the indexed vanishing-error convergence shell `mixedInverseRelativeAmplificationAtScale_sup_tendsto_condition_of_vanishing_error`, the bounded inverse-scale convergence bridge `mixedInverseRelativeAmplificationAtScale_sup_tendsto_condition_of_tendsto_scale_bounded_inverse`, the resolvent inverse-bound envelope bridge `mixedInverseRelativeAmplificationAtScale_sup_tendsto_condition_of_resolvent_inverse_bound`, the small right-inverse resolvent-bound bridge `mixedInverseRelativeAmplificationAtScale_sup_tendsto_condition_of_small_right_inverse`, the source-radius feasible-set/`sSup` bridge `MixedInverseRelativeAmplificationRadiusSet`/`mixedInverseRelativeAmplificationRadiusSup`, the shrinking-radius upper-envelope bridge `mixedInverseRelativeAmplificationRadius_sup_eventually_le_upperEnvelope`, the shrinking-radius lower-witness wrapper `mixedInverseRelativeAmplificationRadius_sup_eventually_lower_le_of_linearized`, and the abstract radius-limit squeeze `mixedInverseRelativeAmplificationRadius_sup_tendsto_condition_of_linearized_witnesses` are checked locally. ## Hidden-hypothesis and weak-component summary

- The new `Norms.lean` layer closes the abstract Definition 6.1/Theorem 6.2 monotone/absolute equivalence for arbitrary norms on `C^n` and now exposes Mathlib's finite complex `Lp` vector norms, finite Holder, finite row-functional dual-q values, several local p-norm comparison bounds, concrete finite-real function wrappers for the chosen local matrix `p`-norm, the exact Euclidean operator-norm bridge for the concrete `p=2` value, endpoint-unified Riesz-Thorin interpolation through `complexMatrixLpNorm_le_rieszThorin_of_interpolationData_all`, and a checked rank/Gram/Frobenius singular-value scaffold with eigenvector realization, `sigma_i <= ||A||_2`, `||A||_2 = sigma_1`, `||A||_F = sqrt (sum_i sigma_i^2)`, `||A||_2 <= ||A||_F <= sqrt(n)||A||_2`, `rank(A) = #{i | sigma_i != 0}`, `||A||_F <= sqrt(rank A)||A||_2`, image orthogonality for `A v_i`, unit normalized left singular vectors for nonzero singular values, zero-image/zero-left-vector branches for zero singular values, the total reconstruction theorem `A v_i = sigma_i u_i`, nonzero left-vector range membership/cardinality, a positive-rank range basis, target-space orthonormal-basis extension, singular-vector expansion, diagonal target-coordinate theorems, a rectangular coordinate-matrix representation theorem, explicit diagonal-or-zero coordinate-matrix entries, concrete unitary factors, and the local rectangular equality `U * Sigma * V^* = A`. These comparison bounds and spectral wrappers still live below some full source theorem layers and must not be advertised as closing remaining source-notation/variant SVD rows or perturbation-limit condition-number rows.
- The Lemma 6.3 rank-one theorem now proves norming-functional existence through Mathlib Hahn-Banach and returns both a linear rank-one map and a concrete finite complex rank-one matrix with local mixed-bound value `1`. It should still be described as a local predicate closure until the repository has the full p-norm/max-sup subordinate norm APIs.
- The generated `chapter_index.md` and `split_primary_contracts.md` line for Theorem 6.4 describes a table-constant caption, but the PDF text verifies Theorem 6.4 is the mixed condition-number theorem on pages 110-111. The report follows the source PDF and records the generated-index mismatch rather than changing the theorem target.
- Maxima in (6.11) now have a source-facing local matrix p-norm max/ratio API through `IsMaxComplexMatrixLpNormValue` and `IsMaxComplexMatrixLpNormRatioValue`, building on the finite complex `Lp` vector norm and row-functional dual-q theorem. For (6.2), local dual functional max/rate predicates, a max-to-least bridge, and a nonempty-dimensional least-value-to-unit/nonzero-ratio maximum bridge exist. For (6.5)-(6.6), a concrete complex matrix-to-map bridge plus nonzero-ratio/unit-sphere maximum bridge exists.
